# big-code-kafka-sec-001: Kafka SASL Authentication Flow Security Analysis

## Task

Trace the Apache Kafka SASL authentication flow from channel creation through mechanism negotiation (PLAIN, SCRAM-SHA-256, OAUTHBEARER, GSSAPI), the challenge-response exchange, principal extraction, to ACL-based authorization. Identify all entry points where untrusted client data enters the SASL subsystem, map the data flow through each authentication mechanism, and analyze the security properties of the authentication and authorization chain.

## Context

- **Repository**: apache/kafka (Java, ~1.2M LOC)
- **Category**: Security Analysis
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/` (authenticator, plain, scram, oauthbearer packages) and `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/` (channel builders)

## Requirements

1. Identify all entry points where untrusted data enters the SASL subsystem (client connections, SASL tokens, handshake requests)
2. Trace the channel builder architecture: how `ChannelBuilders` creates `SaslChannelBuilder` which wires up `SaslServerAuthenticator`
3. Map the SASL handshake protocol: `ApiVersionsRequest` -> `SaslHandshakeRequest` -> mechanism-specific exchange -> authenticated principal
4. Trace at least two mechanism implementations (PLAIN and SCRAM) through their callback handlers to credential verification
5. Identify how `KafkaPrincipal` is extracted post-authentication and how `Authorizer.authorize()` enforces ACLs
6. Document existing mitigations and where they may be insufficient

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file.ext — role in attack surface
...

## Entry Points
1. path/to/entry.ext:function_name — accepts [type of untrusted input]
...

## Data Flow
### Flow 1: [name]
1. Source: path/to/source.ext (untrusted input enters here)
2. Transform: path/to/transform.ext (data is [processed/validated/not validated])
3. Sink: path/to/sink.ext (sensitive operation: [db query/file write/exec/etc.])

## Dependency Chain
[Ordered list of files from entry to sink]

## Analysis
[Detailed security analysis including:
- Vulnerability class (injection, auth bypass, SSRF, etc.)
- Existing mitigations and their gaps
- Attack scenarios
- Recommended remediation]

## Summary
[Concise description of the vulnerability and its impact]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- Attack surface coverage: Did you identify all files in the SASL authentication data flow?
- Entry point identification: Did you find the correct entry points (channel builders, authenticators)?
- Data flow completeness: Did you trace the full path from connection to authorized principal?
- Analysis quality: Is the SASL mechanism architecture correctly described?

- Examined key files in the SASL authentication chain:
  - `ChannelBuilders.java` — factory creating `SaslChannelBuilder` or `PlaintextChannelBuilder` based on `SecurityProtocol`
  - `SaslChannelBuilder.java` — wires up callback handlers per mechanism (PLAIN→`PlainServerCallbackHandler`, SCRAM→`ScramServerCallbackHandler`, OAUTHBEARER→`OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler`, GSSAPI→`SaslServerCallbackHandler`)
  - `SaslServerAuthenticator.java` — core authenticator: handles `ApiVersionsRequest` → `SaslHandshakeRequest` → `SaslAuthenticateRequest` state machine; calls `saslServer.evaluateResponse()` with raw client bytes
  - `PlainSaslServer.java` — parses NUL-delimited `[authzid]\0authcid\0passwd` bytes; delegates to callback handler
  - `PlainServerCallbackHandler.java` — looks up `user_<username>` in JAAS config; uses constant-time comparison
  - `ScramSaslServer.java` — RFC 5802 SCRAM state machine (CLIENT_FIRST → CLIENT_FINAL → COMPLETE)
  - `ScramServerCallbackHandler.java` — fetches `ScramCredential` from `CredentialCache` by username
  - `OAuthBearerSaslServer.java` — parses client initial response, calls

The analysis document has been written to `/logs/agent/solution.md` (797 lines, ~43 KB). Here is a summary of what was covered and the key findings:

---

## What the Analysis Covers

### 1. Channel Builder Architecture
`ChannelBuilders` is a static factory that dispatches to `SaslChannelBuilder`, `SslChannelBuilder`, or `PlaintextChannelBuilder` based on `SecurityProtocol`. For SASL, it builds one `JaasContext` per enabled mechanism and wires callback handlers: `PlainServerCallbackHandler` → PLAIN, `ScramServerCallbackHandler` → SCRAM-SHA-256/512, `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` (or custom) → OAUTHBEARER, `SaslServerCallbackHandler` → GSSAPI.

### 2. SASL Handshake Protocol State Machine
`SaslServerAuthenticator` manages 8 states (INITIAL_REQUEST → HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST → HANDSHAKE_REQUEST → AUTHENTICATE → COMPLETE/FAILED, plus REAUTH_*). Two critical security gates: an **API key whitelist** (only `API_VERSIONS` and `SASL_HANDSHAKE` accepted before auth) and a **mechanism allowlist** (`enabledMechanisms` server-side check on the client-supplied mechanism string). Frame size is capped at 512 KB by default.

### 3. PLAIN
Single-round NUL-delimited `[authzid]\0authcid\0passwd` payload. `PlainServerCallbackHandler` looks up `user_<username>` in JAAS config and uses **`Utils.isEqualConstantTime()`** for timing-safe comparison. **Critical risk:** PLAIN sends passwords in cleartext — requires `SASL_SSL`.

### 4. SCRAM (RFC 5802)
Three-state server (CLIENT_FIRST → CLIENT_FINAL → COMPLETE). All messages parsed with strict regex anchored matches. Server stores only `(storedKey, serverKey, salt, iterations)` — never the plaintext password. Client proof verified with **`MessageDigest.isEqual()`** (constant-time). Nonce replay caught by comparing echoed nonce
... (truncated)

"* @return true if the arrays are equal, or false otherwise\n     */\n    public static boolean isEqualConstantTime(char[] first, char[] second) {\n        if (first == second) {\n            return true;\n        }\n        if (first == null || second == null) {\n            return false;\n        }\n\n        if (second.length == 0) {\n            return first.length == 0;\n        }\n\n        // time-constant comparison that always compares all characters in first array\n        boolean matches = first.length == second.length;\n        for (int i = 0; i < first.length; ++i) {\n            int j = i < second.length ? i : 0;\n            if (first[i] != second[j]) {\n                matches = false;\n            }\n        }\n        return matches;\n    }"

[Cross-Cutting Security Controls](#9-cross-cutting-security-controls)\n10. [Security Findings Summary](#10-security-findings-summary)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Channel Builder Architecture\n\n**Key files:**\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ChannelBuilders.java`\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/SaslChannelBuilder.java`\n\n### Factory Dispatch\n\n`ChannelBuilders` is a pure static factory. `serverChannelBuilder()` and `clientChannelBuilder()` both delegate to the internal `create()` method, which switches on `SecurityProtocol`:\n\n```\nSecurityProtocol.SSL          \u2192 SslChannelBuilder\nSecurityProtocol.SASL_SSL     \u2192 SaslChannelBuilder  (SASL over TLS)\nSecurityProtocol.SASL_PLAINTEXT \u2192 SaslChannelBuilder (SASL over plaintext TCP)\nSecurityProtocol.PLAINTEXT    \u2192 PlaintextChannelBuilder\n```\n\nFor SASL protocols, `create()` builds one `JaasContext` per enabled mechanism and passes them all to `SaslChannelBuilder`. The per-listener config prefix (`listener.name.<name>.`) is stripped via `channelBuilderConfigs()` so mechanism-specific options (e.g., `plain.sasl.jaas.config`) land in the configs map with bare keys.\n\n### Callback Handler Wiring (SaslChannelBuilder)\n\n`SaslChannelBuilder.configure()` maps each mechanism name to a concrete `AuthenticateCallbackHandler`:\n\n| Mechanism         | Server callback handler                              |\n|-------------------|------------------------------------------------------|\n| `PLAIN`           | `PlainServerCallbackHandler`                         |\n| `SCRAM-SHA-256`   | `ScramServerCallbackHandler`                         |\n| `SCRAM-SHA-512`   | `ScramServerCallbackHandler`                         |\n| `OAUTHBEARER`     | `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` (default) or custom |\n| `GSSAPI`          | `SaslServerCallbackHandler`                          |\n\nCustom handlers can be injected via `sasl.server.callback.handler.class` (per-listener, per-mechanism). This is the primary extension point for production OAuthBearer and custom credential stores.\n\n### KafkaPrincipalBuilder Wiring\n\n`ChannelBuilders.createPrincipalBuilder()` reads `principal.builder.class`. If unset or set to `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.class`, a `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder` instance is constructed. Otherwise, the configured class is reflectively instantiated and `configure()` is called on it if it implements `Configurable`. The builder is then stored in `SaslServerAuthenticator`.\n\n**Security implication:** A custom `KafkaPrincipalBuilder` receives the raw `SaslAuthenticationContext` (including the `SaslServer` and optional `SSLSession`), so it can derive principals from JWT claims, SSL certificate attributes, etc. This is the correct extension point; operators must vet any custom implementation.\n\n---\n\n## 2. SASL Handshake Protocol State Machine\n\n**Key file:** `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerAuthenticator.java`\n\n### State Enum\n\n```\nINITIAL_REQUEST               \u2192 first byte(s) received; may be ApiVersions or SaslHandshake\nHANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST \u2192 after valid first Kafka request; ApiVersions or SaslHandshake\nHANDSHAKE_REQUEST             \u2192 after ApiVersionsRequest; must receive SaslHandshake next\nAUTHENTICATE                  \u2192 SASL token exchange in progress\nCOMPLETE                      \u2192 authentication succeeded\nFAILED                        \u2192 authentication failed\n\nREAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE      \u2192 initial state for re-authentication\nREAUTH_BAD_MECHANISM          \u2192 re-auth attempted with a different mechanism\n```\n\n### Message Flow (Initial Authentication)\n\n```\nClient                                           Server (SaslServerAuthenticator)\n  \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 TCP connection \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2192\n  \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 [optional] ApiVersionsRequest (v0-v4) \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2192  handleApiVersionsRequest()\n  \u2190\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 ApiVersionsResponse \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n  \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 SaslHandshakeRequest (mechanism name) \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2192  handleHandshakeRequest()\n  \u2190\u2500\u2500\u2500 SaslHandshakeResponse (enabled mechs) \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n  \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 [loop] SaslAuthenticateRequest \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2192  handleSaslToken() \u2192 saslServer.evaluateResponse()\n  \u2190\u2500\u2500\u2500 [loop] SaslAuthenticateResponse \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n```\n\nFor clients that do not support KIP-43 (pre-0.10 Kafka or non-Kafka clients), the first byte is a GSSAPI token starting with `0x60`. This triggers `InvalidRequestException` at `INITIAL_REQUEST`, which is wrapped into a descriptive error.\n\n### handleKafkaRequest() \u2014 API Key Whitelist\n\n```java\nif (apiKey != ApiKeys.API_VERSIONS && apiKey != ApiKeys.SASL_HANDSHAKE)\n    throw new InvalidRequestException(\"Unexpected Kafka request of type \" + apiKey + \" during SASL handshake.\");\n```\n\nAll API keys except `API_VERSIONS` (18) and `SASL_HANDSHAKE` (17) are rejected before the request body is parsed. This reduces the attack surface during the unauthenticated handshake phase: a malicious client cannot trigger any authenticated API handler before authentication completes.\n\n### handleHandshakeRequest() \u2014 Mechanism Allowlist\n\n```java\nString clientMechanism = handshakeRequest.data().mechanism();  // client-supplied string\nif (enabledMechanisms.contains(clientMechanism)) {\n    // proceed\n} else {\n    throw new UnsupportedSaslMechanismException(\"Unsupported SASL mechanism \" + clientMechanism);\n}\n```\n\nThe mechanism name is a client-supplied string checked against the server-side `sasl.enabled.mechanisms` list. Injection of arbitrary mechanism names is therefore blocked by the allowlist. If rejected, the response includes the list of enabled mechanisms (information disclosure: attackers learn which mechanisms the broker supports).\n\n### Size Limit\n\nAt construction time:\n```java\nsaslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize = (Integer) configs.get(BrokerSecurityConfigs.SASL_SERVER_MAX_RECEIVE_SIZE_CONFIG);\nif (saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize == null)\n    saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize = BrokerSecurityConfigs.DEFAULT_SASL_SERVER_MAX_RECEIVE_SIZE; // 524288 bytes (512 KB)\n```\n\n`NetworkReceive` enforces this limit:\n```java\nif (maxSize != UNLIMITED && receiveSize > maxSize)\n    throw new InvalidReceiveException(\"Invalid receive (size = \" + receiveSize + \" larger than \" + maxSize + \")\");\n```\n\nAny frame exceeding the limit during SASL raises `SaslAuthenticationException` and terminates the connection, providing a coarse defense against oversized credential stuffing requests.\n\n### Re-Authentication\n\nRe-authentication begins in `REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE`. After a full exchange, `ensurePrincipalUnchanged()` is called:\n\n```java\npublic void ensurePrincipalUnchanged(KafkaPrincipal reauthenticatedKafkaPrincipal) throws SaslAuthenticationException {\n    if (!previousKafkaPrincipal.equals(reauthenticatedKafkaPrincipal)) {\n        throw new SaslAuthenticationException(String.format(\n            \"Cannot change principals during re-authentication from %s.%s: %s.%s\", ...));\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis prevents a connected client from re-authenticating as a different user on an established TCP connection, eliminating a potential session-hijacking vector. The mechanism must also remain unchanged (`saslMechanismUnchanged()`).\n\n### Pending State / Error Deferral\n\n`setSaslState(SaslState.FAILED, exception)` does not throw immediately if `netOutBuffer` has pending writes. The exception is held in `pendingException` and thrown only after the outbound response is fully flushed. This ensures the error response is always delivered to the client before the connection is torn down.\n\n---\n\n## 3. PLAIN Mechanism Implementation\n\n**Key files:**\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainSaslServer.java`\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/plain/internals/PlainServerCallbackHandler.java`\n\n### Wire Format (RFC 4616)\n\n```\nmessage = [authzid] UTF8NUL authcid UTF8NUL passwd\n```\n\nThree NUL-delimited (`\\u0000`) UTF-8 fields. `authzid` is optional (empty string if omitted).\n\n### Token Parsing \u2014 `extractTokens()`\n\n```java\nprivate List<String> extractTokens(String string) {\n    List<String> tokens = new ArrayList<>();\n    int startIndex = 0;\n    for (int i = 0; i < 4; ++i) {\n        int endIndex = string.indexOf(\"\\u0000\", startIndex);\n        if (endIndex == -1) {\n            tokens.add(string.substring(startIndex));\n            break;\n        }\n        tokens.add(string.substring(startIndex, endIndex));\n        startIndex = endIndex + 1;\n    }\n    if (tokens.size() != 3)\n        throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Invalid SASL/PLAIN response: expected 3 tokens, got \" + tokens.size());\n    return tokens;\n}\n```\n\nThe loop runs up to 4 iterations but the result must contain exactly 3 elements; otherwise authentication is rejected with a descriptive error. The raw bytes are decoded as UTF-8 **before** splitting on NUL, which is consistent with RFC 4616 but means a malformed UTF-8 sequence would cause a `CharacterCodingException` that surfaces as an authentication failure.\n\n### Credential Verification \u2014 `PlainServerCallbackHandler`\n\n```java\nprotected boolean authenticate(String username, char[] password) throws IOException {\n    if (username == null) return false;\n    String expectedPassword = JaasContext.configEntryOption(jaasConfigEntries,\n            JAAS_USER_PREFIX + username,   // e.g., \"user_alice\"\n            PlainLoginModule.class.getName());\n    return expectedPassword != null && Utils.isEqualConstantTime(password, expectedPassword.toCharArray());\n}\n```\n\n1. **Credential store:** Passwords are stored in the JAAS config as `user_<username>=<password>` options under `org.apache.kafka.common.security.plain.PlainLoginModule`. This means credentials live in broker configuration (file or dynamic config), not in an external database.\n\n2. **Constant-time comparison:** `Utils.isEqualConstantTime()` iterates `first.length` characters regardless of mismatch position, preventing timing-based username/password enumeration:\n\n   ```java\n   boolean matches = first.length == second.length;\n   for (int i = 0; i < first.length; ++i) {\n       int j = i < second.length ? i : 0;\n       if (first[i] != second[j]) matches = false;\n   }\n   return matches;\n   ```\n\n   Note: The length comparison (`first.length == second.length`) is done before the loop, but since `matches` is set to false without early-return, the timing still reveals length differences in theory if the underlying JIT/CPU timing is observable \u2014 though this is an extremely minor concern in practice.\n\n3. **Plaintext password exposure:** PLAIN transmits the password in cleartext. It **must** only be used with `SASL_SSL` (TLS transport). Using `SASL_PLAINTEXT` with PLAIN exposes credentials to any network observer.\n\n### Authorization ID Validation\n\n```java\nif (!authorizationIdFromClient.isEmpty() && !authorizationIdFromClient.equals(username))\n    throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\n        \"Authentication failed: Client requested an authorization id that is different from username\");\n```\n\nIf `authzid` is non-empty, it must match `authcid`. This prevents a PLAIN client from authenticating as `alice` but requesting to act as `admin`, which would be an impersonation attempt.\n\n---\n\n## 4. SCRAM Mechanism Implementation\n\n**Key files:**\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramSaslServer.java`\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramMessages.java`\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramFormatter.java`\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/scram/internals/ScramServerCallbackHandler.java`\n\n### Protocol Overview (RFC 5802)\n\nSCRAM (Salted Challenge Response Authentication Mechanism) performs a mutual authentication exchange using salted HMAC operations; the server never sees the plaintext password.\n\n```\nState: RECEIVE_CLIENT_FIRST_MESSAGE\n  Client \u2192 \"n,,n=<saslname>,r=<client-nonce>[,extensions]\"\n  Server \u2190 \"r=<client-nonce+server-nonce>,s=<base64-salt>,i=<iterations>[,extensions]\"\n\nState: RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE\n  Client \u2192 \"c=<base64-channel-binding>,r=<full-nonce>,p=<base64-client-proof>\"\n  Server \u2190 \"v=<base64-server-signature>\"    (or \"e=<error>\")\n\nState: COMPLETE\n```\n\n### Message Parsing (`ScramMessages`)\n\nAll SCRAM messages are parsed using `java.util.regex.Pattern` anchored matches. The patterns are defined with strict character classes:\n\n```java\nstatic final String VALUE_SAFE = \"[\\\\x01-\\\\x7F&&[^=,]]+\";\nstatic final String SASLNAME   = \"(?:[\\\\x01-\\\\x7F&&[^=,]]|=2C|=3D)+\";\nstatic final String PRINTABLE  = \"[\\\\x21-\\\\x7E&&[^,]]+\";\nstatic final String BASE64     = \"(?:[a-zA-Z0-9/+]{4})*(?:[a-zA-Z0-9/+]{3}=|[a-zA-Z0-9/+]{2}==)?\";\n```\n\n`=2C` and `=3D` are the only allowed escape sequences in SASLNAME (encoding `,` and `=`). This eliminates injection via crafted usernames. A `SaslException` is thrown on mismatch before any credential lookup occurs.\n\n### evaluateResponse() \u2014 CLIENT_FIRST\n\n```java\ncase RECEIVE_CLIENT_FIRST_MESSAGE:\n    this.clientFirstMessage = new ClientFirstMessage(response);\n    // ...\n    String saslName = clientFirstMessage.saslName();\n    String username = ScramFormatter.username(saslName);  // unescape =2C\u2192, and =3D\u2192=\n    NameCallback nameCallback = new NameCallback(\"username\", username);\n    ScramCredentialCallback credentialCallback = new ScramCredentialCallback();\n    callbackHandler.handle(new Callback[]{nameCallback, credentialCallback});\n    this.authorizationId = username;\n    this.scramCredential = credentialCallback.scramCredential();\n    if (scramCredential == null)\n        throw new SaslException(\"Authentication failed: Invalid user credentials\");\n    // authzid check\n    String authorizationIdFromClient = clientFirstMessage.authorizationId();\n    if (!authorizationIdFromClient.isEmpty() && !authorizationIdFromClient.equals(username))\n        throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\n            \"Authentication failed: Client requested an authorization id that is different from username\");\n    // iteration count enforcement\n    if (scramCredential.iterations() < mechanism.minIterations())\n        throw new SaslException(\"Iterations \" + scramCredential.iterations() + \" is less than the minimum ...\");\n```\n\nKey checks at this stage:\n- **Unknown user:** `scramCredential == null` throws a `SaslException` (generic, not a `SaslAuthenticationException`), so the generic error message is returned to the client rather than leaking user existence.\n- **AuthzId mismatch:** rejected with `SaslAuthenticationException` (specific message) \u2014 intentional since the check is logically distinct from credential failure.\n- **Minimum iterations:** Prevents a downgrade attack where an attacker pre-populates ZooKeeper/KRaft with weak credentials using fewer PBKDF2 iterations than the mechanism requires.\n\n### evaluateResponse() \u2014 CLIENT_FINAL\n\n```java\ncase RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE:\n    ClientFinalMessage clientFinalMessage = new ClientFinalMessage(response);\n    if (!clientFinalMessage.nonce().equals(serverFirstMessage.nonce()))\n        throw new SaslException(\"Invalid client nonce in the final client message.\");\n    verifyClientProof(clientFinalMessage);\n    // ...\n```\n\n**Nonce validation:** The client must echo back the full nonce (client-nonce + server-nonce). A mismatch indicates a replay or MITM and is rejected before any cryptographic check.\n\n**Client proof verification (`verifyClientProof`):**\n\n```java\nvoid verifyClientProof(ClientFinalMessage clientFinalMessage) throws SaslException {\n    byte[] expectedStoredKey = scramCredential.storedKey();\n    byte[] clientSignature = formatter.clientSignature(expectedStoredKey, clientFirstMessage,\n                                                        serverFirstMessage, clientFinalMessage);\n    byte[] computedStoredKey = formatter.storedKey(clientSignature, clientFinalMessage.proof());\n    if (!MessageDigest.isEqual(computedStoredKey, expectedStoredKey))\n        throw new SaslException(\"Invalid client credentials\");\n}\n```\n\nThe computation is:\n```\nAuthMessage    = ClientFirstBare + \",\" + ServerFirst + \",\" + ClientFinalWithoutProof\nClientKey      = HMAC(SaltedPassword, \"Client Key\")\nStoredKey      = H(ClientKey)\nClientSignature= HMAC(StoredKey, AuthMessage)\nClientProof    = ClientKey XOR ClientSignature\n\nVerification:\n  computedStoredKey = H(ClientProof XOR ClientSignature) = H(ClientKey) = StoredKey\n```\n\nThe server never reconstructs `SaltedPassword` or `ClientKey`; it only stores and compares `StoredKey`. `MessageDigest.isEqual()` is a constant-time comparison provided by the JDK security library, preventing timing attacks on the proof.\n\n### Credential Cache (`ScramServerCallbackHandler`)\n\n`ScramServerCallbackHandler` fetches `ScramCredential` from `CredentialCache.Cache<ScramCredential>` keyed by username. The credential cache is populated from ZooKeeper (legacy) or KRaft metadata. Each entry contains:\n\n```java\npublic class ScramCredential {\n    private final byte[] salt;\n    private final byte[] storedKey;  // H(ClientKey)\n    private final byte[] serverKey;  // HMAC(SaltedPassword, \"Server Key\")\n    private final int iterations;\n}\n```\n\nThe server never stores `SaltedPassword`, `ClientKey`, or the plaintext password \u2014 only the derived values needed for verification.\n\n### Token-Based SCRAM Authentication (Delegation Tokens)\n\nIf `ScramLoginModule.TOKEN_AUTH_CONFIG` extension is present in the CLIENT_FIRST message, the code path switches to `DelegationTokenCredentialCallback`:\n\n```java\nif (scramExtensions.tokenAuthenticated()) {\n    DelegationTokenCredentialCallback tokenCallback = new DelegationTokenCredentialCallback();\n    callbackHandler.handle(new Callback[]{nameCallback, tokenCallback});\n    if (tokenCallback.tokenOwner() == null)\n        throw new SaslException(\"Token Authentication failed: Invalid tokenId : \" + username);\n    this.authorizationId = tokenCallback.tokenOwner();  // NOT the token ID \u2014 the owner's username\n    this.tokenExpiryTimestamp = tokenCallback.tokenExpiryTimestamp();\n}\n```\n\nThe `authorizationId` is set to the **token owner**, not the token ID. The `tokenExpiryTimestamp` is propagated via `getNegotiatedProperty()` to `SaslServerAuthenticator`, which uses it to compute `sessionLifetimeMs` returned in `SaslAuthenticateResponse`. This is how Kafka enforces token expiry.\n\n---\n\n## 5. OAUTHBEARER Mechanism Implementation\n\n**Key files:**\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerSaslServer.java`\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/OAuthBearerClientInitialResponse.java`\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/unsecured/OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler.java`\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/oauthbearer/internals/unsecured/OAuthBearerUnsecuredJws.java`\n\n### Wire Format (GS2 + RFC 6750)\n\n```\nClientInitialResponse = \"n,\" [\",a=\" authzid] \",\" SEPARATOR kvpairs SEPARATOR SEPARATOR\nkvpairs               = (key \"=\" value SEPARATOR)*\nauth kvpair           = \"auth=Bearer <token>\"\n```\n\n`OAuthBearerClientInitialResponse` parses this via a compiled `Pattern`:\n```java\nprivate static final Pattern CLIENT_INITIAL_RESPONSE_PATTERN = Pattern.compile(\n    String.format(\"n,(a=(?<authzid>%s))?,%s(?<kvpairs>%s)%s\", SASLNAME, SEPARATOR, KVPAIRS, SEPARATOR));\n```\n\nThe token is then extracted from the `auth` key-value pair by `AUTH_PATTERN`:\n```java\nprivate static final Pattern AUTH_PATTERN =\n    Pattern.compile(\"(?<scheme>[\\\\w]+)[ ]+(?<token>[-_~+/\\\\.a-zA-Z0-9]+([=]*))\");\n```\n\nOnly `Bearer` scheme is accepted; any other scheme (`Basic`, etc.) causes a `SaslException`.\n\n### evaluateResponse() Flow\n\n```java\npublic byte[] evaluateResponse(byte[] response) throws SaslException {\n    // Ctrl-A acknowledgement for error path\n    if (response.length == 1 && response[0] == OAuthBearerSaslClient.BYTE_CONTROL_A && errorMessage != null) {\n        throw new SaslAuthenticationException(errorMessage);\n    }\n    OAuthBearerClientInitialResponse clientResponse = new OAuthBearerClientInitialResponse(response);\n    return process(clientResponse.tokenValue(), clientResponse.authorizationId(), clientResponse.extensions());\n}\n```\n\nThe `\\x01` (Ctrl-A) byte is the RFC 7628 abort mechanism: if the server sends an error JSON, the client echoes `\\x01` and the server throws the deferred error. This two-round-trip error protocol means the error message is logged (at DEBUG level) and re-thrown but never double-logged.\n\n### process() \u2014 Token Validation\n\n```java\nprivate byte[] process(String tokenValue, String authorizationId, SaslExtensions extensions) throws SaslException {\n    OAuthBearerValidatorCallback callback = new OAuthBearerValidatorCallback(tokenValue);\n    callbackHandler.handle(new Callback[]{callback});\n    OAuthBearerToken token = callback.token();\n    if (token == null) {\n        errorMessage = jsonErrorResponse(callback.errorStatus(), ...);\n        return errorMessage.getBytes(StandardCharsets.UTF_8);  // challenge to client\n    }\n    if (!authorizationId.isEmpty() && !authorizationId.equals(token.principalName()))\n        throw new SaslAuthenticationException(\"Authentication failed: Client requested an authorization id (\" +\n            authorizationId + \") that is different from the token's principal name (\" + token.principalName() + \")\");\n    // ...\n    tokenForNegotiatedProperty = token;\n    complete = true;\n}\n```\n\n**Error message contains both the requested authzid and the token principal.** This is a `SaslAuthenticationException`, which propagates its message to the client in the `SaslAuthenticateResponse`. An operator using a custom handler that embeds sensitive identifiers in the principal name should be aware that mismatches expose both values to the client.\n\n### Default Unsecured Validator \u2014 NOT FOR PRODUCTION\n\n`OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` validates tokens where `alg=none` (unsigned JWTs):\n\n```java\n// From OAuthBearerUnsecuredJws:\nString alg = Objects.requireNonNull(header().get(\"alg\"), \"...\").toString();\nif (!\"none\".equals(alg))\n    throw new OAuthBearerIllegalTokenException(...);\nString digitalSignatureSplit = splits.get(2);\nif (!digitalSignatureSplit.isEmpty())\n    throw new OAuthBearerIllegalTokenException(...);\n```\n\nA JWT with `alg=none` carries no cryptographic guarantee of authenticity. **Any client that can connect to the broker can fabricate an arbitrary principal name by constructing a trivial unsigned JWT.** This handler is explicitly documented as development/testing only and must never be used in production. Production deployments must configure `sasl.server.callback.handler.class` to a handler that validates JWT signatures against a trusted JWKS endpoint.\n\n### Extensions Validation\n\n```java\nprivate Map<String, String> processExtensions(OAuthBearerToken token, SaslExtensions extensions) throws SaslException {\n    OAuthBearerExtensionsValidatorCallback extensionsCallback = new OAuthBearerExtensionsValidatorCallback(token, extensions);\n    callbackHandler.handle(new Callback[]{extensionsCallback});\n    if (!extensionsCallback.invalidExtensions().isEmpty()) {\n        String errorMessage = String.format(\"Authentication failed: %d extensions are invalid! They are: %s\",\n            extensionsCallback.invalidExtensions().size(),\n            Utils.mkString(extensionsCallback.invalidExtensions(), \"\", \"\", \": \", \"; \"));\n        throw new SaslAuthenticationException(errorMessage);\n    }\n    return extensionsCallback.validatedExtensions();\n}\n```\n\nThe error message includes the names of invalid extensions. If the default handler does not implement `OAuthBearerExtensionsValidatorCallback` (throws `UnsupportedCallbackException`), extensions are silently ignored for backwards compatibility. Custom handlers that do validate extensions should ensure that extension names themselves do not contain sensitive data before including them in error messages.\n\n---\n\n## 6. GSSAPI/Kerberos Mechanism\n\n**Key files:**\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/SaslServerCallbackHandler.java`\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosShortNamer.java`\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/kerberos/KerberosName.java`\n\n### GSSAPI SaslServer Creation\n\nFor GSSAPI, the service principal is extracted from the broker's Kerberos `Subject`:\n\n```java\nfinal String servicePrincipal = SaslClientAuthenticator.firstPrincipal(subject);\nKerberosName kerberosName = KerberosName.parse(servicePrincipal);\nreturn SecurityManagerCompatibility.get().callAs(subject, () ->\n    Sasl.createSaslServer(saslMechanism, servicePrincipalName, serviceHostname, configs, saslServerCallbackHandler));\n```\n\nThe JVM's built-in GSSAPI/Kerberos SASL provider handles the multi-round-trip token exchange.\n\n### AuthorizeCallback Handling\n\n`SaslServerCallbackHandler.handleAuthorizeCallback()` is the only callback needed for GSSAPI (in addition to `RealmCallback`):\n\n```java\nprivate void handleAuthorizeCallback(AuthorizeCallback ac) {\n    String authenticationID = ac.getAuthenticationID();\n    String authorizationID  = ac.getAuthorizationID();\n    LOG.info(\"Successfully authenticated client: authenticationID={}; authorizationID={}.\", ...);\n    ac.setAuthorized(true);\n    ac.setAuthorizedID(authenticationID);  // always uses authcid, not authzid\n}\n```\n\nThe authorized ID is **always** set to `authenticationID` regardless of the requested `authorizationID`. This means Kerberos service-name impersonation (S4U2Proxy / constrained delegation at the SASL layer) is not supported. The `authorizationID` passed by the client is silently overridden with `authenticationID`.\n\n### Principal Name Transformation (KerberosShortNamer)\n\nAfter authentication, `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.applyKerberosShortNamer()` runs the Kerberos principal through `auth_to_local` rules:\n\n```java\nKerberosName kerberosName = KerberosName.parse(authorizationId);\nString shortName = kerberosShortNamer.shortName(kerberosName);\nreturn new KafkaPrincipal(KafkaPrincipal.USER_TYPE, shortName);\n```\n\n`KerberosShortNamer` parses rules matching the pattern:\n```\nDEFAULT | RULE:[ncomps:format](match-regex)s/search/replace/[g][L|U]\n```\n\nRules are applied in order; the first match is used. If no rule matches, `NoMatchingRule` is thrown. The `DEFAULT` rule maps the primary component if the realm matches, or maps `serviceName@REALM` \u2192 `serviceName` for cross-realm cases. Rule parsing validates the entire rule string against `RULE_PARSER`; malformed rules raise `IllegalArgumentException` at broker startup, not at runtime.\n\n---\n\n## 7. KafkaPrincipal Extraction\n\n**Key files:**\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/authenticator/DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.java`\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/KafkaPrincipal.java`\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/auth/SaslAuthenticationContext.java`\n\n### Build Path\n\nAfter `saslServer.isComplete()` transitions the state to `COMPLETE`, `KafkaChannel.principal()` calls `SaslServerAuthenticator.principal()`:\n\n```java\npublic KafkaPrincipal principal() {\n    Optional<SSLSession> sslSession = transportLayer instanceof SslTransportLayer ?\n            Optional.of(((SslTransportLayer) transportLayer).sslSession()) : Optional.empty();\n    SaslAuthenticationContext context = new SaslAuthenticationContext(\n            saslServer, securityProtocol, clientAddress(), listenerName.value(), sslSession);\n    KafkaPrincipal principal = principalBuilder.build(context);\n    if (ScramMechanism.isScram(saslMechanism) &&\n            Boolean.parseBoolean((String) saslServer.getNegotiatedProperty(ScramLoginModule.TOKEN_AUTH_CONFIG))) {\n        principal.tokenAuthenticated(true);\n    }\n    return principal;\n}\n```\n\nThe `SaslAuthenticationContext` carries the live `SaslServer` instance, giving custom `KafkaPrincipalBuilder` implementations access to all negotiated properties (e.g., the full `OAuthBearerToken` for claim-based authorization).\n\n### DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.build()\n\n```java\n} else if (context instanceof SaslAuthenticationContext) {\n    SaslServer saslServer = ((SaslAuthenticationContext) context).server();\n    if (SaslConfigs.GSSAPI_MECHANISM.equals(saslServer.getMechanismName()))\n        return applyKerberosShortNamer(saslServer.getAuthorizationID());\n    else\n        return new KafkaPrincipal(KafkaPrincipal.USER_TYPE, saslServer.getAuthorizationID());\n}\n```\n\nFor all non-GSSAPI SASL mechanisms, the principal is `User:<authorizationId>` where `authorizationId` is:\n\n| Mechanism    | Source of authorizationId                                 |\n|--------------|-----------------------------------------------------------|\n| PLAIN        | `authcid` (username extracted from NUL-delimited payload) |\n| SCRAM        | `username` (or token owner if delegation token)           |\n| OAUTHBEARER  | `token.principalName()` (claim from JWT)                  |\n| GSSAPI       | `authenticationID` after Kerberos short-name mapping      |\n\nFor PLAINTEXT connections, `build()` returns `KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS` (`User:ANONYMOUS`).\n\n### KafkaPrincipal Equality\n\n```java\npublic boolean equals(Object o) {\n    // ...\n    return principalType.equals(that.principalType) && name.equals(that.name);\n}\n```\n\nEquality is based on `(principalType, name)` only. `tokenAuthenticated` is **not** part of equality. Two principals with the same type and name compare equal regardless of whether one was authenticated via a delegation token. The `tokenAuthenticated` flag is used for auditing and downstream checks (e.g., restricting operations to token-authenticated sessions) but cannot be relied on for ACL comparison.\n\n### KafkaPrincipal Transport (Inter-Broker)\n\n`DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder` also implements `KafkaPrincipalSerde`:\n\n```java\npublic byte[] serialize(KafkaPrincipal principal) {\n    DefaultPrincipalData data = new DefaultPrincipalData()\n        .setType(principal.getPrincipalType())\n        .setName(principal.getName())\n        .setTokenAuthenticated(principal.tokenAuthenticated());\n    return MessageUtil.toVersionPrefixedBytes(DefaultPrincipalData.HIGHEST_SUPPORTED_VERSION, data);\n}\n```\n\nWhen `KafkaPrincipal` is forwarded between brokers (e.g., for consumer group coordination), it is serialized and deserialized. The deserializer validates the version field against `LOWEST_SUPPORTED_VERSION` and `HIGHEST_SUPPORTED_VERSION`, throwing `SerializationException` on out-of-range values.\n\n---\n\n## 8. ACL-Based Authorization\n\n**Key files:**\n- `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/authorizer/Authorizer.java`\n- `metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/metadata/authorizer/StandardAuthorizerData.java`\n- `metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/metadata/authorizer/StandardAuthorizer.java`\n- `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/AuthHelper.scala`\n\n### Request Context Assembly\n\n`SocketServer.Processor` assembles a `RequestContext` that carries the authenticated principal:\n\n```java\nval context = new RequestContext(header, connectionId, channel.socketAddress,\n    Optional.of(channel.socketPort()), channel.principal, listenerName,\n    securityProtocol, channel.channelMetadataRegistry.clientInformation,\n    isPrivilegedListener, channel.principalSerde)\n```\n\n`channel.principal` is the `KafkaPrincipal` built by `SaslServerAuthenticator.principal()`. Every request processed by `KafkaApis` carries this immutable context.\n\n### AuthHelper \u2014 Convenience Layer\n\n```scala\ndef authorize(requestContext: RequestContext, operation: AclOperation,\n              resourceType: ResourceType, resourceName: String, ...): Boolean = {\n    authorizer.forall { authZ =>\n        val resource = new ResourcePattern(resourceType, resourceName, PatternType.LITERAL)\n        val actions = Collections.singletonList(new Action(operation, resource, refCount, logIfAllowed, logIfDenied))\n        authZ.get.authorize(requestContext, actions).get(0) == AuthorizationResult.ALLOWED\n    }\n}\n```\n\n`authorizer.forall` returns `true` when no authorizer is configured (open mode). With an authorizer configured, authorization is delegated to it. `KafkaApis` calls `authHelper.authorize()` for every sensitive operation (Produce, Fetch, CreateTopics, etc.).\n\n### StandardAuthorizerData.authorize() \u2014 Decision Logic\n\n```java\npublic AuthorizationResult authorize(AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext, Action action) {\n    KafkaPrincipal principal = baseKafkaPrincipal(requestContext);\n\n    // Superusers bypass all ACLs, including DENY ACLs\n    if (superUsers.contains(principal.toString())) {\n        rule = SuperUserRule.INSTANCE;   // always ALLOWED\n    } else if (!loadingComplete) {\n        throw new AuthorizerNotReadyException();\n    } else {\n        rule = findAclRule(matchingPrincipals(requestContext), clientAddress, action);\n    }\n    logAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule);\n    return rule.result();\n}\n```\n\n**Super-user check:** `superUsers` contains strings of the form `\"User:alice\"` (the result of `KafkaPrincipal.toString()`). A super-user is granted `ALLOWED` for every action, including those covered by explicit DENY ACLs. Super-users are configured via `super.users` broker config.\n\n**ACL precedence (findAclRule):** The default rule precedence is:\n1. DENY (explicit deny wins over any allow)\n2. ALLOW (explicit allow)\n3. No matching ACL \u2192 DENIED (default-deny)\n\n### matchingPrincipals()\n\n```java\nstatic Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals(AuthorizableRequestContext context) {\n    KafkaPrincipal sessionPrincipal = context.principal();\n    KafkaPrincipal basePrincipal = sessionPrincipal.getClass().equals(KafkaPrincipal.class)\n        ? sessionPrincipal\n        : new KafkaPrincipal(sessionPrincipal.getPrincipalType(), sessionPrincipal.getName());\n    return Set.of(basePrincipal, WILDCARD_KAFKA_PRINCIPAL);  // {\"User:alice\", \"User:*\"}\n}\n```\n\nBoth the literal principal and the wildcard `User:*` are included in the matching set. An ACL granting `User:*` on a resource applies to all users. When a custom `KafkaPrincipalBuilder` returns a subclass of `KafkaPrincipal` (e.g., with group membership embedded), the authorizer works with a **base** principal stripped of subclass-specific data \u2014 unless the authorizer itself is also customized to understand the subclass.\n\n### baseKafkaPrincipal()\n\n```java\nstatic KafkaPrincipal baseKafkaPrincipal(AuthorizableRequestContext context) {\n    KafkaPrincipal sessionPrincipal = context.principal();\n    return sessionPrincipal.getClass().equals(KafkaPrincipal.class)\n        ? sessionPrincipal\n        : new KafkaPrincipal(sessionPrincipal.getPrincipalType(), sessionPrincipal.getName());\n}\n```\n\nFor audit log purposes, the base principal is used (same behavior as `matchingPrincipals`). Subclass fields are not audited unless a custom authorizer overrides `logAuditMessage`.\n\n### Authorizer Interface \u2014 Threading Model\n\nThe `Authorizer` interface documents:\n- `authorize()` is synchronous and called on the request thread. Implementations must not block on remote I/O.\n- ACL mutations (`createAcls`, `deleteAcls`) are asynchronous and return `CompletionStage`.\n- `start()` returns per-listener futures; the broker does not accept connections on a listener until its future completes.\n- The implementation must be thread-safe.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Cross-Cutting Security Controls\n\n### 9.1 JAAS Login Module Allowlist\n\n`JaasContext.throwIfLoginModuleIsNotAllowed()` checks the configured login module class name against a deny-list read from the system property `org.apache.kafka.disallowed.login.modules`:\n\n```java\nprivate static final String DISALLOWED_LOGIN_MODULES_DEFAULT =\n    \"com.sun.security.auth.module.JndiLoginModule,com.sun.security.auth.module.LdapLoginModule\";\n```\n\nThis is a direct mitigation for CVE-2021-44228 (Log4Shell) and its variant CVE-2021-45046, which demonstrated that JNDI lookups in JAAS configuration could be exploited for remote code execution. Operators can extend the deny-list by setting the system property. If a required module is incorrectly blocked, the system property can be cleared \u2014 but this should be done cautiously.\n\n### 9.2 Error Message Sanitization\n\nIn `SaslServerAuthenticator.handleSaslToken()`:\n\n```java\n} catch (SaslException e) {\n    // DO NOT include error message from the `SaslException` in the client response since it may\n    // contain sensitive data like the existence of the user.\n    String errorMessage = \"Authentication failed during \" +\n            reauthInfo.authenticationOrReauthenticationText() +\n            \" due to invalid credentials with SASL mechanism \" + saslMechanism;\n    buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(requestContext, new SaslAuthenticateResponse(\n            new SaslAuthenticateResponseData()\n            .setErrorCode(Errors.SASL_AUTHENTICATION_FAILED.code())\n            .setErrorMessage(errorMessage)));\n    throw new SaslAuthenticationException(errorMessage, e);\n}\n```\n\n`SaslException` (the generic SASL error) produces a fixed error string; the internal exception message is **not** forwarded to the client. `SaslAuthenticationException` (application-level error) is forwarded \u2014 this is intentional for cases where the application needs to communicate a specific reason (e.g., invalid token format). Mechanism implementers are explicitly warned in Javadoc:\n\n> _\"This method may throw `SaslAuthenticationException` to provide custom error messages to clients. But care should be taken to avoid including any information in the exception message that should not be leaked to unauthenticated clients.\"_\n\n### 9.3 Delegation Token Model\n\nDelegation tokens use SCRAM as a transport mechanism but authenticate against the token store rather than the user credential cache. The `authorizationId` is set to the **owner** of the token (not the token identifier), so ACL checks apply to the owner's permissions. The `tokenExpiryTimestamp` is surfaced as a negotiated property and drives `sessionLifetimeMs` in the handshake response, which tells the client when to initiate re-authentication.\n\n### 9.4 SASL_SSL vs SASL_PLAINTEXT\n\n| Protocol         | PLAIN      | SCRAM  | OAUTHBEARER | GSSAPI |\n|------------------|------------|--------|-------------|--------|\n| `SASL_PLAINTEXT` | \u26a0\ufe0f Unsafe  | \u2713 Safe | \u2713 Safe      | \u2713 Safe |\n| `SASL_SSL`       | \u2713 Safe     | \u2713 Safe | \u2713 Safe      | \u2713 Safe |\n\nPLAIN with `SASL_PLAINTEXT` sends the password unencrypted over TCP and must not be used in production. SCRAM and OAUTHBEARER are safe over plaintext transport because no secret is transmitted directly. GSSAPI is safe because it uses Kerberos tickets, not passwords.\n\nFor `SASL_SSL`, SSL client authentication is deliberately disabled by default for SASL listeners unless configured with a listener-specific prefix (`listener.name.<name>.ssl.client.auth`). This design decision prevents SASL and mTLS from conflicting.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Security Findings Summary\n\n| # | Finding | Severity | Location |\n|---|---------|----------|----------|\n| F1 | **OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler accepts `alg=none` JWTs** \u2014 any client can forge any principal name | Critical (if deployed in production) | `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler`, `OAuthBearerUnsecuredJws` |\n| F2 | **PLAIN over SASL_PLAINTEXT** exposes plaintext passwords to network observers | High (configuration risk) | `PlainSaslServer`, broker config |\n| F3 | **SaslHandshakeResponse leaks enabled mechanisms** to unauthenticated clients | Low / Info | `SaslServerAuthenticator.handleHandshakeRequest()` |\n| F4 | **GSSAPI ignores requested authorizationId** \u2014 always uses authenticationID | Design / Low | `SaslServerCallbackHandler.handleAuthorizeCallback()` |\n| F5 | **OAuthBearer authzid/principal mismatch message exposes both values** to the client | Low | `OAuthBearerSaslServer.process()` |\n| F6 | **Default `Authorizer.authorizeByResourceType()`** is O(n) over all ACLs without caching | Performance / Low | `Authorizer.authorizeByResourceType()` default impl |\n| F7 | **Super-user bypasses DENY ACLs** \u2014 no way to deny a super-user | Design | `StandardAuthorizerData.authorize()` |\n| F8 | **`Utils.isEqualConstantTime()` leaks password length** via early exit on `second.length == 0` | Very Low | `Utils.isEqualConstantTime()` |\n| F9 | **JAAS blocklist is system-property-controlled** \u2014 can be cleared by a JVM argument | Defence-in-depth | `JaasContext.throwIfLoginModuleIsNotAllowed()` |\n| F10 | **`tokenAuthenticated` excluded from `KafkaPrincipal.equals()`** \u2014 token-auth sessions and password-auth sessions are indistinguishable via equals | Design / Low | `KafkaPrincipal.equals()` |\n\n### Positive Security Controls Observed\n\n| Control | Location |\n|---------|----------|\n| Constant-time password comparison (PLAIN) | `Utils.isEqualConstantTime()` |\n| Constant-time proof comparison (SCRAM) | `MessageDigest.isEqual()` in `verifyClientProof()` |\n| SCRAM minimum iteration count enforcement | `ScramSaslServer.evaluateResponse()` |\n| SCRAM nonce replay prevention | `clientFinalMessage.nonce()` vs `serverFirstMessage.nonce()` |\n| SCRAM server never stores plaintext password | `ScramCredential` (storedKey + serverKey only) |\n| API key whitelist during unauthenticated handshake | `handleKafkaRequest()` |\n| Mechanism allowlist check | `handleHandshakeRequest()` |\n| SASL frame size limit (512 KB default) | `NetworkReceive` + `saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize` |\n| Principal immutability during re-authentication | `ensurePrincipalUnchanged()` |\n| Mechanism immutability during re-authentication | `saslMechanismUnchanged()` |\n| Generic error messages for credential failures | `SaslServerAuthenticator.handleSaslToken()` |\n| AuthzId \u2260 AuthcId rejection (PLAIN, SCRAM, OAUTHBEARER) | All three `evaluateResponse()` implementations |\n| JNDI/LDAP login module blocklist | `JaasContext.throwIfLoginModuleIsNotAllowed()` |\n| Super-user not loaded until metadata is available | `StandardAuthorizerData.loadingComplete` |\n\n---\n\n*Analysis based on Apache Kafka source code in `/workspace`.
